  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2250a23e-6eb9-4c45-afbc-f3f38f70ef28'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText5232300402137642415" style="display:none"><b>The epic conclusion to the internationally bestselling Nevernight Chronicle from New York Times bestselling author Jay Kristoff.</b><br /><br />The greatest games in Godsgrave’s history have ended with the most audacious murders in the history of the Itreyan Republic.<br /><br />Mia Corvere, gladiatii, escaped slave and infamous assassin, is on the run. Pursued by Blades of the Red Church and soldiers of the Luminatii legion, she may never escape the City of Bridges and Bones alive. Her mentor Mercurio is now in the clutches of her enemies. Her own family wishes her dead. And her nemesis, Consul Julius Scaeva, stands but a breath from total dominance over the Republic.<br /><br />But beneath the city, a dark secret awaits. Together with her lover Ashlinn, brother Jonnen and a mysterious benefactor returned from beyond the veil of death, she must undertake a perilous journey across the Republic, seeking the final answer to the riddle of her life. Truedark approaches. Night is falling on the Republic for perhaps the final time.<br /><br />Can Mia survive in a world where even daylight must die?<br /><br />New York Times and internationally bestselling author Jay Kristoff’s writing has been praised by critics and readers alike and has won many awards, including four Aurealis Awards, an ABIA, and David Gemmell Morningstar and Legend awards.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff">lgbtq-ff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2436783918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7471190574257910346">I had thought my return to this series would be as easy as falling back in a friendly old dream, as effortless as curtains parting and meeting again on either side of an opera performance, a lever being pulled, one set whisked to the rafters and another dropped to the stage.<br/><br/>Yet, when I finished reading <em>Darkdawn</em>, I found myself moved by two contrary currents: my love for this series, appearing in the fragile wisp of my memory very much like its bright old self, and the realization—like a shock of</span>
  <span id="freeText7471190574257910346" style="display:none">I had thought my return to this series would be as easy as falling back in a friendly old dream, as effortless as curtains parting and meeting again on either side of an opera performance, a lever being pulled, one set whisked to the rafters and another dropped to the stage.<br /><br />Yet, when I finished reading <em>Darkdawn</em>, I found myself moved by two contrary currents: my love for this series, appearing in the fragile wisp of my memory very much like its bright old self, and the realization—like a shock of cold water—that it had gradually burned away like a sea fog beneath the sun. There’s that distant feeling of familiarity still, but it’s soft around the edges, mushy, like it’s crumbling away. I almost wish I hadn’t read this book, so I could remain within the circumference of the past—back when nothing could have persuaded me to believe that my giddy enthusiasm for this series would one day become vague, entirely shrouded by the mists of time.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br />The need for revenge has been a violent fire within Mia Corvere for eight years, and in the gladiatii arena, its flames had flared hot and blue. As a result, Julius Scaeva is dead, and her brother, Jonnen, whom she thought dead, is alive and safe. The world was supposed to work the way it had always been intended to work, running smoothly on all cylinders. But if Scaeva’s evil had been purely volatile, he might have not been as deadly as plague. Instead, he was calculating, and calculating men seldom dwell among the dead.<br /><br />Scaeva appears to his daughter with a placating offer, to join his side and share his power, and in anyone else, it might have looked like kinship, but Mia couldn’t see it as anything so benign. Mia wanted to visit on him a cataclysm of nightmares that would leave him spinning through darkness forever. But a new realization tiptoes toward her, unfaltering and ugly: Mia and Scaeva were as alike as leaves, and maybe she was always meant to be as much of a monster, and he was only the instrument.<br /><br />But more complicated than Mia’s unthwarted pursuit of vengeance: Jonnen’s remembrance of his sister is muddied-up below the waterline alongside his late mother, and although his savior, Mia now seems to him baleful and outlandish and cruel, and even more inexpiable, his father’s murderess. Tric, it seems, has dragged his mortal limbs through fearful darkness to come back for Mia, carrying a destiny, but his infantile hope quickly curdles into something jagged and despairing when he learns that Mia’s new lover is none other than Ashlinn, the woman who killed him. Tric and Ashlinn are like twin harpies of past and present hovering always by Mia, and her heart was at war with itself. And they were all on steel tracks thundering inevitably on into a perilous, inky tunnel ahead.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    YOUR VENGEANCE IS AS THE SUNS, MIA. IT SERVES ONLY TO BLIND YOU.
  </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Darkdawn’s company is like a strong tonic. Bracing—and best to eschew altogether if you can’t handle the kick. Beguiled by the series’ theatrical unrepentance and intractable style, I found myself falling under its spell. This time, however, the same spell hung on me, yet I felt weightless.<br /><br />The stakes in this installment are mostly smaller than in the series' opener and sequel. <em>Darkdawn</em> is a harrowing read, but not even half as much so as its predecessors. The unforced pace drags, and the plot is rather such an unrelenting onslaught of fight scenes, sex, bawdiness, it becomes numbing. The result is an unbalanced, unwieldy beast that could have been streamlined some.<br /><br />The acerbic angst, the verbal excess, the deadpan laughs—it turns out—are not an endlessly renewable energy source. Like in the series books before it, the author likes to drop in from the sky in his narratorial guise with cute self-referential footnotes and dramatic asides, even toying with the edges of meta and making fun of his own wordy tendencies—a habit I previously found illuminating, charming and clever, but which had worn thin like a scrap of limp rope thrown over a branch you can hardly grapple onto, and begun to require a great deal of emotional labor. Kristoff lays it on a little too thick too often, and his efforts to transform nearly every observation into something either hilarious or profound yields many overwritten lines and dilutes the story’s power to persuade us. Throughout, I kept reflecting: if this is how desultory I feel after three chapters, then how desultory can I expect to feel after twenty more?<br /><br />Every now and then, the story kicks into a new gear, and the shift feels right, only for a twist to happen, sending the plot, regrettably, in a different direction, away from I once most relished about the series: the intricate plotting, gallows humor and murky moral grays.<br /><br />Also a tad deflating: in my memory, the dynamics between the characters—specifically, the romance—projected such an impression of solidity and wholeness which—to me, at least—seemed to have been leached away in this book, leaving them just pale noise. The snide, taunting edge of Ashlinn’s impenitence annoyed me, Mia’s endless ping-ponging between Tric and Ash aggravated me to no end, and it’s nearly impossible to reconcile with Tric’s vitality as a character knowing how the story ends. The only saving grace was Jonnen’s presence and the dynamics of two siblings who lived different childhoods, yet were shaped in such similar ways.<br /><br />The conclusion, once it settles, feels—if not satisfying—than weirdly inevitable. I think I would have felt more strongly about it if the author has chosen instead to upend the board game and send the pieces flying—completely subverting all expectations.<br /><br />I guess you either die without having read the finale of your favorite series or live long enough to be sorely disappointed.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7471190574257910346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2212231081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212231081" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212231081?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250073044" href="/book/show/37587820-darkdawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=f-f">f-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=erotic-scenes">erotic-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212231081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3275982140854843525"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566599306i/28041418._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br/>2.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159863289?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars,” she replied. “I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son.” Mia leaned forward and looked the man in the eye. “I am the war you cannot win.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Nevernight</i> is about a girl, desperate to learn the truth</span>
  <span id="freeText3275982140854843525" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566599306i/28041418._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159863289?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars,” she replied. “I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son.” Mia leaned forward and looked the man in the eye. “I am the war you cannot win.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Nevernight</i> is about a girl, desperate to learn the truth of her family, and willing to do anything it takes to seek her revenge.<br><br><i>Godsgrave</i> is about a young woman, learning more of her and her family’s past, and willing to do anything it takes to survive.<br><br><i>Darkdawn</i> is about a powerful woman, learning what she wants in this life, and willing to do anything to protect the ones she loves.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“As promised, her birth you’ve witnessed, her life you’ve lived. All that remains is her death.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Hi, my name is Melanie, and I truly think this trilogy is a masterpiece. Most of you know, this is a very beloved series in the book community, and with good reason, it truly is a story that somehow has completely bled into my very own heart and feels completely a part of me. Seeing Mia, seeing her struggles and defeats, seeing her power and victories, seeing everything ugly and beautiful in between, it has been an honor, friends. A true honor and one that I won’t forget.<br><br>This is going to be a hard book to review, mostly because it is the concluding book of a trilogy, but also just because I am too emotionally invested. Seeing Mia be a recruit for the red church, to seeing her being a gladiator willing to risk it all, to seeing her deal with what it means to get close to your absolution, it’s all so beautiful and it all evokes so many emotions from me that are beyond words.<br><br>I guess I should take a minute to talk about all the side characters, even though I truly could gush about Mia Corvere forever. But Mia has so many enemies, but just as many people who truly have grown to love her. This series has such an extensive cast of side characters, but they all feel so different and so fleshed out.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it’s a terrible thing, Dona Mia, when the ones who should love you best leave you for the wolves.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Especially Mercurio. You all know that I have loved this grumpy old man for many years, but what a bright, shining light in this final installment. I love what was done with his character so much! And let’s all be honest here, we all love seeing when the hard, grumpy one ends up being the soft, sweet one. Mercurio and Mia’s relationship and found family is the stuff of dreams. And the constant theme of family being the people you choose is so beautifully executed throughout this entire series, but it is especially highlighted in <i>Darkdawn</i>.<br><br>And not to get into anything spoiler, but you all know I love reading about sibling relationships, especially when it is an older sister protecting a little brother. Also, I have been very open about this series having one of my favorite f/f relationships of all time, and I was living my best life, gentle friends, truly. All of the relationship dynamics are expertly done; romantic, platonic, familial, all perfection.<br><br>The author has been very open about the ending of this book and how it was going to be pretty sad, but the ending truly surpassed everything I could have imagined. I find it very rare for me to be completely satisfied with the ending of a beloved series, and somehow Jay Kristoff was able to pull off perfection.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Sometimes the past won’t just die. Sometimes you have to kill it.”</i>
</b><br>Overall, this series just means a lot to me, and I truly love it wholeheartedly. And before you all ask, yes, I did cry a lot while reading. First, because I truly am still not ready to say goodbye, but also because Jay Kristoff does not pull back the punches, and this shit hurts, friends. But I was crying with a smile on my face, this I swear. And all the footnotes? I feel like I could write a separate review for the spectrum of emotions they were able to evoke from me. I just love this series so much, and I love Mia more than any words I could string together for a sappy review. Lastly, anyone who loves the UK versions of this series? You all are going to geek out while reading this book. Okay, love you, bye.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> talk of child sex slavery in the past, graphic violence, gore, blood depiction, torture, loss of a loved one, death, murder, a lot of alcohol consumption, talk of rape in the past, talk of pedophilia in the past, talk of suicide, many threats of rape, sexual assault (unwanted touching), and abandonment. This is a very dark, adult book! Please use caution while reading, and make sure you are in a safe headspace. <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a> at <a href="http://www.jaironside.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">JA Ironside</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="3275982140854843525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2517345724?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2517345724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17526032464895398953"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576386083i/28613974._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote>I have read my way through 315 books to bring you my <b>
  <u>
    <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ugRPM83WE2k' rel='nofollow noopener'>Top 10 Books of the Year (video)</a>
  </u>
</b>.<br/><br/>Now you know that this one made the cut, check out <b>
  <u>
    <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ugRPM83WE2k' rel='nofollow noopener'>my video review</a>
  </u>
</b> to see the others! <blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567375358i/28085602._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>What doesn't kill me had better fucking run.</i>
</blockquote>Mia Corere - once a rich little girl - experienced <b>her entire world shift on its axis </b>whern Consul Julius Scaeva murdered her father.<br/><br/>In her quest for revenge, Mia has leapt from lonely orphan girl to assassin to gladiatii. <br/><br/>And once she secured her positi</span>
  <span id="freeText17526032464895398953" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576386083i/28613974._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>I have read my way through 315 books to bring you my <b>
  <u>
    <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ugRPM83WE2k" rel="nofollow noopener">Top 10 Books of the Year (video)</a>
  </u>
</b>.<br><br>Now you know that this one made the cut, check out <b>
  <u>
    <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ugRPM83WE2k" rel="nofollow noopener">my video review</a>
  </u>
</b> to see the others! <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567375358i/28085602._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>What doesn't kill me had better fucking run.</i>
</blockquote>Mia Corere - once a rich little girl - experienced <b>her entire world shift on its axis </b>whern Consul Julius Scaeva murdered her father.<br><br>In her quest for revenge, Mia has leapt from lonely orphan girl to assassin to gladiatii. <br><br>And once she secured her position, she managed to murder her enemy - leader of the Republic...<b>
  <i> or so she thought.</i>
</b><br><br>Turns out Consul Julius Scaeva - murderer of her father and countless others - escaped, but not for long.<blockquote>
  <i>This is who I am. I'm not a hero. I'm a vengeful, selfish bitch. </i>
</blockquote>If there is one thing -<b> one absolute thing</b> - you can be certain about...it's that if Mia decides to kill you, nothing - not friends, family, guards, armies or even Gods will be able to stand in her way.<blockquote>
  <i>I am the war you cannot win.</i>
</blockquote>What in the hell am I supposed to do with my life now??? Ahhhh... let me dwell in my misery. <br><br>In short - this book was truly - and I mean truly -<b> an absolute stunner. </b><br><br>This whole series - not a dud in the lot. <br><br>This round Mia takes her younger brother (Jonnen) under her wing, and he is ever the spiteful brat that she was. <br><br>It was a <b>fun, humanizing dynamic </b>that I'm forever grateful that Kristoff added to this series. <blockquote>
  <i>You never know what can break you until you're falling apart. You never miss your shadow until you're lost in the dark.</i>
</blockquote>I also loved how Mia, despite her strength and cunning, was heartbreakingly human. Ashlinn, Mercurio and Jonnen all rounded out her character beautifully. <br><br>And, above all,<b> I loved her attitude</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>If you wanted a saviour, perhaps you should've picked a girl who believes this world is worth saving.</i>
</blockquote>There's something so refreshing to finally (FINALLY) have a "Chosen One" who goes <i>- ehhh. I'd rather not. </i><br><br>My only regret? That this series is finished. I really have nothing left to do in this world.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2696621151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696621151" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696621151?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008180089" href="/book/show/39281503-darkdawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696621151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15588149711567686809"><b>O’gentlefriends, <i>Darkdawn</i> concluded <i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i> trilogy on a bloody high note, and it’s not implausible for me to say that this has become my favorite book in the series.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Don't fuck with librarians, young lady. We know the power of words." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Each installment within the series can be classified as Mia’s journey throughout her life; <i>Nevernight</i> as Mia’s book of birth, <i>Godsgrave</i> as Mia’s book of life, and <i>Darkdawn</i> as Mia’s book death. Don’t worry, if you’re reading this withou</span>
  <span id="freeText15588149711567686809" style="display:none"><b>O’gentlefriends, <i>Darkdawn</i> concluded <i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i> trilogy on a bloody high note, and it’s not implausible for me to say that this has become my favorite book in the series.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Don't fuck with librarians, young lady. We know the power of words." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Each installment within the series can be classified as Mia’s journey throughout her life; <i>Nevernight</i> as Mia’s book of birth, <i>Godsgrave</i> as Mia’s book of life, and <i>Darkdawn</i> as Mia’s book death. Don’t worry, if you’re reading this without any knowledge of the series, that’s not a spoiler; the first page within the first book of the series has mentioned that Mia died. Now, the specifics leading towards it, and whether Mia’s death is a lie or truth, I’ll leave that for you to find out for yourself. <i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i>, in a way, is Mia’s revenge story told by an unnamed narrator that the reader didn’t know, not until they’ve read <i>Darkdawn</i> anyway. I can’t tell you anything specific about the story in <i>Darkdawn</i> except that it continues immediately from where <i>Godsgrave</i> left off, and <i>Darkdawn</i> really finished Mia’s story. What I can tell you, however, is what made the book worked so well for me.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “And the more I live it, the more I realize “deserve” has nothing to do with this life. Blessings and curses fall on the wicked and the just alike. Fair is a fairy tale. Nothing's claimed by those who don't want it, and nothing's kept by those who won't fight for it. So let's fight.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /> <br />I personally think that <i>Darkdawn</i> is the best book of the trilogy. I was on a short vacation for the past couple of days; let me tell you that putting this book down was an immensely difficult task to do. There’s a ridiculously alluring strength within Kristoff’s writing that compelled me to find out whether Mia will truly die or not. A barrage of revelations was forwarded immediately to readers—some of them being the identity of the unnamed narrator and the origin of the Darkins—within the first quarter of the book, and there are so many characterizations plus developments happening to the characters throughout the trilogy this late into the series that I hugely enjoyed reading. One of my most favorite changes implemented into this book is how the narrative has shifted into multi-perspective rather than Mia’s only POV. The multi-perspective inclusion made the story felt bigger in scope, and most importantly, it definitely made me care for many of the characters within the series rather than only a few. Kristoff really took every event from the previous two books into account; the characters, even those who I thought would only serve as minor characters, played a role in subtly enriching the scope and complexities of the series. The banter between friends, the camaraderie, the in-depth characterization, and the gradual character development; all unified to make the book more emotional than I expected it would be and I loved it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “To live in the hearts of those we leave behind is to never die. And to burn in the memories of our friends is to never say goodbye.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Out of all the books in the trilogy, <i>Darkdawn</i>’s story progression felt structured like traditional epic fantasy; filled with travels around the world, gathering comrades for the upcoming final battle, dangerous seafaring, and heartwarming interactions between the characters—both returning and new—that displayed how far they’ve have come and grown to care about each other. Although each book in the series felt a bit different from each other, they never lose the themes that acted as a constant compass for the plotlines: revenge, familia, friendship, responsibilities, and love persists even more so within this book. I also loved how Kristoff conveyed the lesson that pain shaped maturity and you don't know what you got till it’s gone. A lot of creativities were involved in Kristoff’s storytelling style. And I’m not just speaking exclusively about the unconventional page-format found in Mia’s Shadowsteps usage or how well-written the book was. I’m talking about the incredible fourth-wall-breaking application within the narrative where Kristoff made fun of his own writing and more. The correlation between some books in Itreya and some books in our real-life was superb. These shouldn’t have worked but they did, and every moment of reading them made me smile with glee. Furthermore, I found the footnotes in <i>Godsgrave</i> too much to my liking; it fills me with joy that the frequency of the footnotes in <i>Darkdawn</i> has been reduced significantly compared to the previous two books.<br /> <br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Pretty warriors can’t fight for shit. You can’t know how sweet it is to breathe ’til you’ve had your ribs broken. You can’t appreciate being happy ’til someone has made you cry. And there’s no point blaming yourself for the kickings life gives you. Just think about how much it hurt, and how much you don’t want to feel that way again. And that’ll help you do what you need to do the next time to win.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /> <br />Before I closed my review, I would like to add that the action sequences in <i>Darkdawn</i> were by far the best in the entire trilogy. Mia’s Shadowsteps continues to hook my attention, amazing sea battles that exceeded my expectations; Kristoff has also painted scenes of obsidian carnage in the last quarter of the book. Honestly, all the action scenes were incredibly immersive, well-written, and can be visualized vividly. Full of stakes, blood, and ruin; Mia’s stormy waltz of vengeance, in my opinion, concluded satisfyingly. If you look at the US cover art of <i>Darkdawn</i>, you can observe glimpses of what’s to come here. Expect unveiled hatred, rage, and palpable tension in this finale; you shall be satisfied.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “I am a daughter of the dark between the stars. I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son. I am the war you cannot win.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /> <br />There’s nothing left to say other than to say that I loved <i>Darkdawn</i> very much. I have a feeling the events that occurred in this book might divide the fans of the series; fortunately, it only made me love the book and the trilogy even more. <i>Darkdawn</i> is an astonishingly brilliant conclusion to <i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i>. Every page of this book was seductive, compelling, and I found this concluding installment to be greatly satisfying. Without a doubt, <i>Darkdawn</i> will be included in my annual end-of-the-year list as one of my favorite reads of the year. Well done, Jay Kristoff. I look forward to reading the beginning of your upcoming new series, <i>Empire of the Vampire</i>, next year. <br /><br />Until then, goodnight, gentlefriends.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Fear was Can't.<br />Fear was Won't.<br />But fear wasn't ever a choice.<br />To never fear was to never hope. Never love. never live. To never fear the dark was to never smile as the dawn kissed your face. To never fear solitude was to never know the joy of a beauty in your arms.<br />Part of having is the fear of losing.<br />Part of creating is the fear of it breaking.<br />Part of beginning is the fear of your ending.<br />Fear is never a choice.<br />Never a choice.<br />But letting it rule you is.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Series Review:</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>Nevernight</i>: <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696620084?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br /><i>Godsgrave</i>: <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696621023?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br /><i>Darkdawn</i>: <b>
  <u>5/5 stars</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i>: <b>
  <u>13.5/15 stars</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780008180089/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/09/11/book-review-darkdawn-the-nevernight-chronicle-3-by-jay-kristoff/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>

<div id="review_2712703982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712703982" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2712703982?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✨ A ✨  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=arcs-e-arcs-alcs">arcs-e-arcs-alcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=three-stars">three-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=2019-release">2019-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2712703982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5458743237842816508">O, gentlefriends it has taken me a while to gather my thoughts on this one.<br/><br/><blockquote>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars,” she replied. “I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son.” Mia leaned forward and looked the man in the eye. “I am the war you cannot win.”</blockquote><br/><br/>As some of you will notice, I changed my rating from 4 stars to 3. <br/><b>SPOILERS FOR BOOK 1 & 2 ⤵</b><br/><br/>We start off exac</span>
  <span id="freeText5458743237842816508" style="display:none">O, gentlefriends it has taken me a while to gather my thoughts on this one.<br><br><blockquote>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars,” she replied. “I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son.” Mia leaned forward and looked the man in the eye. “I am the war you cannot win.”</blockquote><br><br>As some of you will notice, I changed my rating from 4 stars to 3. <br><b>SPOILERS FOR BOOK 1 &amp; 2 ⤵</b><br><br>We start off exactly where Godsgrave ended with Mia in the arena escaping after the murder of Scaeva and Duomo.<br><br>This book was about both Mia getting her revenge once and for all and also her journey, along with new and old friends, to the crown of the moon. <br><br><i>
  <b>You’re more than just a killer. If you open your arms to it, you’re the girl who can right the fucking sky.</b>
</i><br><br>She discovers many things in this book, finally getting answers to her questions about the darkin. And realising the cost of her revenge and not willing to lose anyone else because of it. <br><br>{I don't want to go into too much detail about the plot because it will just spoil your reading experience.}<br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>“To live in the hearts we leave behind is to never die,” Tric said softly.</i>
</b><br><br>I really enjoyed reading about Mia and Jonnen. He was honestly the best part of this, he reminded me so much of Matthias Helvar from Six of Crows duology. And I loved how hard Mia worked to make Jonnen understand that they were siblings and that she cared for him. This sibling relationship was one of the better parts of this story.<br><br>A lot of this book was fantastic, but there was a big amount of disappointment. <br><br>Mia's revenge plot was definitely the reason <b>I</b> was more invested in this series but when <i>Darkdawn</i> took a turn into typical <i>YA-chosen-one</i> territory, that's where it lost me. <br><br>What I loved the most about the first two books was the skill in which Kristoff managed to shock the socks off his readers with his twists and endings. And while the ending of <i>this</i> book will satisfy many readers, it just didn't do it for me. <br><br>Let me not even get into how bland the romance was *huge eye roll*. I was not a fan of the Tric/Ashlynn tension. <br><br>Trust me I was expecting this to be a five star read but there was <i>too much</i> lacking. <br><br>The ending was so disappointing and I was literally sitting and staring at the last page thinking <i>‘....is this it?’</i> : /<br><br>And while this finale was disappointing I'm still glad I read these books. I will not forget these precious characters so easily and book 1 will always be a favourite of mine. I just wished this book was executed better. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563473877ra/27849216.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>Special thank you to my good friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027" rel="nofollow noopener">Fares</a> for recommending this series and for reading Nevernight with me and for always being available for my rants and theories. Fares, if it wasn't for you, this series probably would have sat unread on my shelf for a good couple of years. ILY bro<br><br><br><br><b>‹ Publication Date: 3 September 2019 ›</b><br><br><i>« Quotes might change after final publication. »</i><br><br>________<br><i>ARC received from publisher via edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br>________<br><b>My reviews for:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712701280" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712704041" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5458743237842816508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3284981553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3284981553" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3284981553?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_2786845211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2786845211" />
    <a title="Umairah | Sereadipity" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73298985-umairah-sereadipity"><img alt="Umairah | Sereadipity" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548509728p2/73298985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2786845211?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Umairah | Sereadipity" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Umairah | Sereadipity" href="/user/show/73298985-umairah-sereadipity">Umairah | Sereadipity</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2786845211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10268621205500416579"><strong>Darkdawn</strong> was the <strong>dramatic conclusion</strong> to the Nevernight trilogy full of <strong>humour</strong>, <strong>murderous angst</strong> and the<strong> indomitable sass</strong> of Mia Corvere.<br/><br/><b>Plot: 4/5<br/>Characters: 5/5<br/>Writing: 5/5 </b><br/><br/>In this book, <strong>Mia</strong> continued her journey to <strong>revenge</strong> while also discovering more about <strong>darkin lore</strong> and the mysterious <strong>Crown of the Moon</strong>. Mia came a long way in this book, even more than in Nevernight and Godsgrave as she finally discovered the <strong>truth</strong> about herself and accepted the<strong> path</strong> laid out for her. She realised her life coul</span>
  <span id="freeText10268621205500416579" style="display:none"><strong>Darkdawn</strong> was the <strong>dramatic conclusion</strong> to the Nevernight trilogy full of <strong>humour</strong>, <strong>murderous angst</strong> and the<strong> indomitable sass</strong> of Mia Corvere.<br /><br /><b>Plot: 4/5<br />Characters: 5/5<br />Writing: 5/5 </b><br /><br />In this book, <strong>Mia</strong> continued her journey to <strong>revenge</strong> while also discovering more about <strong>darkin lore</strong> and the mysterious <strong>Crown of the Moon</strong>. Mia came a long way in this book, even more than in Nevernight and Godsgrave as she finally discovered the <strong>truth</strong> about herself and accepted the<strong> path</strong> laid out for her. She realised her life could be about<strong> more than revenge</strong> and built up her own, new <strong>family</strong> around her. And of course, she had her usual <strong>daring</strong>, <strong>sarcasm</strong> and tendency to get herself into the craziest situations and find the craziest ways of getting out of them.I loved her relationship with <strong>Jonnen</strong> and despite everything she was such<strong> a caring big sister</strong> and it was sweet to watch their trust in each other grow. I also loved Mia and <strong>Ashlinn</strong>'s relationship and I just wanted them to be happy together! <br /><br />Other <strong>out of context</strong> things that I loved about Darkdawn:<br /> <br />	- <b>Cloud Corleone</b><br />	-<strong>Tric</strong> vs <strong>Ashlinn</strong><br />	-<strong>Mr Kindly</strong><br />	-Chapter <strong>35</strong> (the most heart-rending chapter I've ever read)<br />	-All the characters <strong>mocking the footnotes</strong><br />	-The<strong> library</strong> in the Quiet Mountain<br /><br />As you can tell, there were many things that I loved and I've given the previous books in the series five stars. So <strong>why did I give Darkdawn four stars?</strong> Well, it was<strong> the ending</strong>. It was a good and<strong> fitting</strong> ending in many ways but <strong>I just didn't connect with it</strong>. I expected to feel emotional as I finished one of my favourite series but<strong> I didn't feel anything</strong>. My main issue was with the scene of the final battle just before the very end because it didn't make sense to me and it didn't feel right. It all happened<strong> too quickly</strong> and I don't think it was <strong>powerful</strong> as it could have been. When I got to the end I just thought: <em>'Is that it?'</em>.<br /><br />Although I had a slight issue with the ending and I don't think it was as <strong>brilliant</strong> as Nevernight or Godsgrave, I did enjoy Darkdawn overall and <strong>Mia's story will always have a place in my heart</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Thank you St. Martin's Press to for providing me with a review copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All opinions expressed are my own.</em> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10268621205500416579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2788335870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2788335870" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2788335870?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008180089" href="/book/show/39281503-darkdawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review">reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788335870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3637872896203671816"><i>
  <b>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars. I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son. I am the war you cannot win.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Revenge is a dish best served with death, copious amounts of it dealt out by a merciless hand. And we all knew this would end in blood. It had to. Mia has been working towards her bloody goals for a long time and for the first time they are within</span>
  <span id="freeText3637872896203671816" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“I am a daughter of the dark between the stars. I am the thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. I am the vengeance of every orphaned daughter, every murdered mother, every bastard son. I am the war you cannot win.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Revenge is a dish best served with death, copious amounts of it dealt out by a merciless hand. And we all knew this would end in blood. It had to. Mia has been working towards her bloody goals for a long time and for the first time they are within her reach.<br /><br />She has become a total bad-ass. Well, she was one from the beginning except now her skills match her arrogant attitude. She knew what she had inside of her; she knew what she could become: she just had to get there. I had no doubts that she would get everything she desired because of her raw passion and anger. It’s unrelenting and totally unstoppable. And that’s her greatest strength and she knows exactly how to use it. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“My name is Mia Corvere. Blade of the Red Church. Champion of the Venatus Magni. Chosen of the Dark Mother and Queen of Scoundrels. Never call me girl again.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Her enemies were once held in reverence by herself. She once looked up to them and was impressed by their power and talents. Now she has more than them. She is stronger. She is smarter. And she is going to kill them all like a master slaying an apprentice. And for the first time her opponents truly started to take her seriously. Her achievements speak for themselves and have earnt her a huge amount of begrudgingly potent respect. <br /><br />So when death comes knocking they will be ready for it. And what transpires are some of the most well written actions scenes I've ever had the pleasure to read. They are raw and they are real. And I think Kristoff has truly honed his craft as a writer here. The blade he wields has a very sharp edge and he uses it to deadly effect to bring this series to a close with a bloody flourish. Nothing is left unanswered. And all blood is spilt. <br /><br />I have no complaints. This book was everything it needed to be to bring this trilogy to a close. And what a trilogy it is. One of the best in the genre. It’s pretty much action layered on top of fantastic storytelling with complex characters from the get-go. And that may sound like a very generic and basic thing to say about a book, but how often do authors truly get this formula right? There’s almost always something wrong, some small way in which a writer could up their game or a major way if the book is trash. <br /><br />So I will end by simply stating this: there is no way this book could have been any better.<br /><br />_________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="3637872896203671816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2920950553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2920950553" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2920950553?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2920950553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12026831965593327931"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/09/02/darkdawn-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/>Nevernight ★★★★★<br/>Godsgrave ★★★★★<br/>Darkdawn ★★★<br/><br/> <b>
  <i>“Fear has its uses,” he replied. “Fear is what keeps the dark from devouring you. Fear is what stops you joining a game you cannot hope to win.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>🌟 So people saw my 3 stars rating on GR and were wondering and O, friends, it is time to give you all the answer and let me remind you of a few things, my rating for books 1 and 2 was 5 stars (book 2 felt more like a 4 but I can be generous sometimes). No one was </span>
  <span id="freeText12026831965593327931" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/09/02/darkdawn-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br />Nevernight ★★★★★<br />Godsgrave ★★★★★<br />Darkdawn ★★★<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>“Fear has its uses,” he replied. “Fear is what keeps the dark from devouring you. Fear is what stops you joining a game you cannot hope to win.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 So people saw my 3 stars rating on GR and were wondering and O, friends, it is time to give you all the answer and let me remind you of a few things, my rating for books 1 and 2 was 5 stars (book 2 felt more like a 4 but I can be generous sometimes). No one was surprised as me by the rating of this one.<br /><br />🌟 I don’t know why I keep thinking of Jay as a new author to me, I was surprised by the fact that I read 8 of his books after finishing this one (This series, The Illuminae files, Aurora Rising and LIFEL1K3) and let me tell you something, there is a formula that Mr.Kristoff uses and I liked it before but this time it was too much as I will explain.<br /><br />🌟 I am not going to talk about the plot as it is hard to do so without spoiling and this will be spoiler-free! There was something good in each book of the series, book 1 was the best but was a bit hard to get into, book 2 was easier to get into but the characters and settings were not as interesting, this one has the best beginning, we revisit the characters from the first book, the settings is great and it was easy to get into without the purple prose in Nevernight.<br /><br />🌟 I felt the author did a great job at first and many things were explained from the start, usually, the books are slow at first and pick up toward the end. This time it was the opposite, I would say the first 20% were excellent and then it became a cluster of too much smut and sarcasm!<br /><br />🌟 I have gained a little experience in knowing how will books do and mark my words, this currently has a 4.57 average rating but it will drop, this will be as controversial as book 1, some will love it and some will hate it and other won’t even finish it!<br /><br />🌟 The writing was not bad per se, the problem is that too much was given at first and so the rest of the book felt like fillers to add pages! nothing much happens, it becomes so repetitive and boring, it was just smut scene after smut scene and the sarcasm that I liked in the first two books was not the same in this one. I felt it was overused and unnecessary in many places, it started getting on my nerves, to be honest! If you check the previous books reviews, you would see that people enjoyed the darkness and the sarcasm, I think Mr.Kristoff did the logical thing and increased the dose this time! but too much of anything can be lethal. And the footnotes in this one were more tamed than book 2. There was a portion of the book were they disappeared altogether and then they popped up later in a funny way.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> “ How do you kill a monster without becoming one yourself?” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 There were not many new characters this time and that was better, I like the characters that we already had and so we got to know more about them. If you like the romance in book 2 you will probably like this one, if you prefer the one in book 1 then you will probably think of this as meh!<br /><br />🌟 We finally get to understand more about the world and I like the world-building in this one which is not complicated but is unique.<br /><br />🌟 The plot in this one was not as good as the first two books, that jaw-dropping, mind-blowing twists were not found this time and I was able to predict the ending of this one as I messaged my friend Azrah with some theories while reading it! Also, Mr.Kristoff found a way to praise himself in this one and although I thought it was funny at first, I did not think it was something important to the story but apparently that thing was important in the story and you may be thinking “what is he talking about??!” and I know it sounds like I am hallucinating but you will understand when you read this one.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>“When all is blood, blood is all.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 Summary: I think I am forgetting some things that I wanted to say but this became another huge rant so bear with me xD. The book was not as good as the first two books, it delivered an excellent introduction but was lost after that in sex and sarcasm. It was predictable but with good characters and writing.<br /><br />you can get the book from here: <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12026831965593327931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078351368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18122545302346674465">so. darkdawn. the final book in my favorite series. the long awaited death of mis corvere. how do i review a book this important to me? i cant put my feelings into words, but for the sake of this arc i'll try.<br/><br/>i have to say, this entire series has an imprint in my soul. back in 2017, when i read nevernight for the first time, i fell in love. with the world, with mister kindly, with mia, with the unapologetic brutality, heart and life mia corvere has. i've always said how i feel like this series w</span>
  <span id="freeText18122545302346674465" style="display:none">so. darkdawn. the final book in my favorite series. the long awaited death of mis corvere. how do i review a book this important to me? i cant put my feelings into words, but for the sake of this arc i'll try.<br /><br />i have to say, this entire series has an imprint in my soul. back in 2017, when i read nevernight for the first time, i fell in love. with the world, with mister kindly, with mia, with the unapologetic brutality, heart and life mia corvere has. i've always said how i feel like this series was tailor-made for me. it has every trope that i love, the main character i've spent years looking for and the world i always wanted. so i cant do this series or my feelings toward it justice, since it doesn't feel like reviewing a book, it feels like reviewing a part of me. <br /><br /><b>the arc of this trilogy is beautiful.</b> it doesnt overstay its welcome (though i would gladly read more), it's cohesive and has a very defined beginning, middle and end. as our revealed narrator said themself, it's birth and life and death. three books, the tale of mia corvere. and fuck, what a beautiful tale it was.<br /><br />while this is definitely a worthy ending to the series, there might be things here some people don't like, and that's fine. for example, if you weren't really interested in the darkin lore, and that whole mystery, then you'll probably not like this book very much. But if you're like me, who's been fascinated by this world and its mythology, who couldn't wait for the answers, then i'm saying it right now: you will love this book. <br /><br />if you haven't guessed it by now, i absolutely fucking loved this. it built up on every good part of the previous two, reveled in it, and then continued on to smash them together in an unforgettable climax. mark my words: <b>the world is not ready for darkdawn</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />--------<br />first thoughts<br /><br /><br />not gonna lie, man, that might have been the best book i've ever read. a perfect ending to a beautifully flawed trilogy. i'll cherish them forever<br /><br /><br />i may or may not be crying my eyes out like a baby. you'll never know.<br /><br /><br /><br />---------<br /><br />having the final book in my favorite series of all time coming out this year and not being able to read it is driving me INSANE</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3061029353?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785174612" href="/book/show/48556045-darkdawn">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3061029353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11417179136692360173">4.5****<br/><br/><i>You never miss your shadow until you’re lost in the dark.</i><br/><br/>So I don’t even know where to start this review as I’m just so sad that my journey with Mia has ended. I feel like I have been punched in the gut and now I don’t know what to do as the series has ended. But it ended spectacularly and now I am just sitting here contemplating the end of the series.<br/><br/>In this book things are coming to the great finale. Mia makes her own discoveries and old and new characters from the books come together f</span>
  <span id="freeText11417179136692360173" style="display:none">4.5****<br /><br /><i>You never miss your shadow until you’re lost in the dark.</i><br /><br />So I don’t even know where to start this review as I’m just so sad that my journey with Mia has ended. I feel like I have been punched in the gut and now I don’t know what to do as the series has ended. But it ended spectacularly and now I am just sitting here contemplating the end of the series.<br /><br />In this book things are coming to the great finale. Mia makes her own discoveries and old and new characters from the books come together for the final showdown. There was political intrigue, Gods and lots of death and gore leading to great revelations and epic fight scenes. This book invoked a range of emotions in me: shock at discoveries, curiosity of learning about the history, sadness and best of all- humour. This book still had the same sense of wit and sarcasm as the previous books and I absolutely adored it. All of the scenes between Mercurio and Mia were my favourite due to their wittiness and love to one another. <br /><br />This was not the full five stars as I didn’t care much for the romance bickering and a whining child 😂. Other than that this was a brilliant ending to a fantastic series with one of my favourite main characters. I’m just so sad it’s over.<br /><br /><i>”Don’t fuck with librarians young lady. We know the power of words.”</i></span>

<div id="review_2986337229" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986337229" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=03-hall-of-shame">03-hall-of-shame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=32-made-me-want-to-pull-my-hair-out">32-made-me-want-to-pull-my-hair-out</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2986337229&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986337229" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093798129870269359">Love triangles. The bane of my existence. God, how I hate them. Particularly when I’m on the wrong side.<br/><br/>I’m telling you, Tric deserved so much better and I can’t get over how disappointed I am because of the hand Mr. Kristoff dealt him. He came back from the dead for Mia only to get it continuously shoved in his face how the girl he loves is now with his murderer. <br/><br/>“I know you can smell her on me.” <br/><br/>Good fucking God, have you not one shred of decency you stupid cow? (I really want to call Ash some</span>
  <span id="freeText17093798129870269359" style="display:none">Love triangles. The bane of my existence. God, how I hate them. Particularly when I’m on the wrong side.<br /><br />I’m telling you, Tric deserved so much better and I can’t get over how disappointed I am because of the hand Mr. Kristoff dealt him. He came back from the dead for Mia only to get it continuously shoved in his face how the girl he loves is now with his murderer. <br /><br />“I know you can smell her on me.” <br /><br />Good fucking God, have you not one shred of decency you stupid cow? (I really want to call Ash something else here but I’m trying to swear less. (Ha!))<br />I know, I know, she cried then (boohoo), really regretted it and actually apologized to Tric for sticking a knife in his chest. Well, guess what? Too fucking little, too fucking late, bitch. And of course good old Tric, bless his heart, ended up doing everything in his power to make sure Mia got her HEA and actually forgave the backstabbing bitch for killing him. Well, good for him but this girl holds grudges. Uh-huh!<br /><br />I’m wondering whatever Tric did to Kristoff for him to turn the guy into the doormat of the series?<br /><br />Anyway. There’s not much else I have to say about this, sadly. There were some good things, like seeing Sid and Singer again. Cloud cracked me up. Liked learning more about Jonnen. But I have to be honest, the whole Ashlinn/Tric situation was a constant thorn in my side and ruined my fun. I tried looking past it, but to no avail. I started skimming a good deal of the book because I just...checked out. I didn’t want to read anymore about Ash’s lips and her eyes and her freckles and how she smelled and tasted and for the love of all things holy, enough already! I just stopped caring about any of the characters. Mia’s unapologetic stance, Ashlinn’s taunts...When the two main characters annoy you so, it’s really hard to keep giving a damn about the story in its entirety and whether the characters live or die. Which brings me to the ending. So disappointing. Just for once, I would’ve liked for someone to actually stay dead. You know, I'm usually the type of person who really likes a HEA - but it has to fit with the story and here, to me, it just didn't.<br /><br />Book one will forever remain one of my favorites and I will remember book two fondly, but this one? I’m gonna pretend it doesn’t exist.</span>
